Biotechnol. 30, 83–89 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3362">14</a></sup>, together with two out-group species (<i>Arabidopsis</i><sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="The Arabidopsis genome initiative. Analysis of the genome sequence of the flowering plant Arabidopsis thaliana. Nature 408, 796–815 (2000)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3369">22</a></sup> and grape<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Velasco, R . et al. A high quality draft consensus sequence of the genome of a heterozygous grapevine variety. PLoS ONE 2, e1326 (2007)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3373">23</a></sup>), were analyzed using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C.J. &amp; Roos, D.S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3377">20</a></sup> to circumscribe sets of orthologous genes. In a first step, species-by-species as well as within species BLASTP (E-value: 1e-5) was performed to identify reciprocal best hit pairs between species (putative orthologs), as well as sets of genes more closely related within than between species (sets of co-orthologs, also known as in-paralogs). This reciprocal best hit matrix served as the basis for ortholog definition using OrthoMCL<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Li, L., Stoeckert, C.J. &amp; Roos, D.S. OrthoMCL: identification of ortholog groups for eukaryotic genomes. Genome Res. 13, 2178–2189 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3381">20</a></sup> (inflation [I] parameter = 1.5). Orthologous groups were then organized into species-specific and higher taxonomic level groups by requiring that at least one sequence from each clade under comparison be present in the intersecting set. Sets of single-copy orthologs with representation in all species were selected and fourfold degenerate sites of these genes were used to construct a phylogenetic tree across nine species using MRBAYES<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="Huelsenbeck, J.P. &amp; Ronquist, F. MRBAYES: Bayesian inference of phylogenetic trees. Bioinformatics 17, 754–755 (2001)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3385">42</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec21">Identification and phylogenetic analysis of NBS-LRR genes.</h3><p>A diverse set of 1,120 protein sequences from the highly conserved NBS domain was built from a panel of cloned legume NBS sequences (B.D.R., unpublished data), as well as published NBS domains from Mt1.0 and Poplar<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Ameline-Torregrosa, C. et al. Identification and characterization of nucleotide-binding site-leucine-rich repeat genes in the model plant Medicago truncatula. Plant Physiol. 146, 5–21 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3397">43</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="Kohler, A. et al. Genome-wide identification of NBS resistance genes in Populus trichocarpa. Plant Mol. Biol. 66, 619–636 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3400">44</a></sup>. These sequences were used as a TBLASTN query against CaGA v1.0 to identify all NBS genomic regions.</p><p>Nucleotide sequences were translated into amino acids, imported into the CIPRES Science Gateway<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="Miller, M.A., Pfeiffer, W. &amp; Schwartz, T. Creating the CIPRES Science Gateway for inference of large phylogenetic trees (Gateway Computing Environments Workshop, 14 November 2010; IEEEXplore, 2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3407">45</a></sup> and aligned using the E-INS-i search strategy in MAFFT<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="Katoh, K. &amp; Toh, H. Parallelization of the MAFFT multiple sequence alignment program. Bioinformatics 26, 1899–1900 (2010)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3411">46</a></sup>. Alignments were converted into relaxed phylip format. Phylogenetic trees were generated with RAxML<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 47" title="Stamatakis, A. RAxML-VI-HPC: maximum likelihood-based phylogenetic analyses with thousands of taxa and mixed models. Bioinformatics 22, 2688–2690 (2006)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3415">47</a></sup> with the JTT substitution matrix, a Gamma distribution (+G), empirical base frequencies (+F) and automatic bootstrap criteria (Maximum Likelihood). Models were evaluated in MEGA5 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 48" title="Tamura, K. et al. MEGA5: molecular evolutionary genetics analysis using maximum likelihood, evolutionary distance, and maximum parsimony methods. Mol. Biol. Evol. 28, 2731–2739 (2011)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3418">48</a>). <i>Medicago</i> NBS domains were included as an outgroup.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec22">Synteny analysis.</h3><p>Synteny blocks between the genomes of chickpea and other legumes were computed by SyMAP<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Soderlund, C., Nelson, W., Shoemaker, A. &amp; Paterson, A. SyMAP: A system for discovering and viewing syntenic regions of FPC maps. Genome Res. 16, 1159–1168 (2006)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3433">49</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="Soderlund, C., Bomhoff, M. &amp; Nelson, W. SyMAP v3.4: a turnkey synteny system with application to plant genomes. Nucleic Acids Res. 39, e68 (2011)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3436">50</a></sup>. Genomic sequences were first aligned using promer/MUMmer<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Kurtz, S. et al. Versatile and open software for comparing large genomes. Genome Biol. 5, R12 (2004)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3440">31</a></sup>. Raw anchors resulting from MUMmer were clustered into (putative) gene anchors, filtered using a reciprocal top-2 filter and used as input to the synteny algorithm<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="Soderlund, C., Nelson, W., Shoemaker, A. &amp; Paterson, A. SyMAP: A system for discovering and viewing syntenic regions of FPC maps. Genome Res. 16, 1159–1168 (2006)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3444">49</a></sup>. The algorithm constructs maximal-scoring anchor chains based on a given gap penalty, and also searches a range of gap penalties to generate the longest chains subject to several quality criteria, which are based on the Pearson correlation coefficient applied to the anchors in the chain as well as the anchors in its bounding box. The chains are not required to be entirely colinear and may incorporate local inversions relative to the overall chain orientation.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec23">Identification of SSRs and SNPs.</h3><p>MIcroSAtellite<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="Thiel, T., Michalek, W., Varshney, R.K. &amp; Graner, A. Exploiting EST databases for the development and characterization of gene derived SSR-markers in barley (Hordeum vulgare L.). Theor. Appl. Genet. 106, 411–422 (2003)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3456">51</a></sup> was used to mine SSRs in the chickpea genome, and used for primer design<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Varshney, R.K. et al. Draft genome sequence of pigeonpea (Cajanus cajan), an orphan legume crop of resource-poor farmers. Nat. Biotechnol. 30, 83–89 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3460">14</a></sup> (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2491#MOESM1">Supplementary Tables 15 and 16</a>). For identification of SNPs based on transcript sequence data, high-quality transcript reads were mapped to the genome assembly using TopHat, allowing two mismatches. SAMtool v 0.18 (ref. <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 52" title="Li, H. et al. The sequence alignment/map format and SAMtools. Bioinformatics 25, 2078–2079 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3466">52</a>) with default parameters was used to call SNPs (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2491#MOESM5">Supplementary Table 17</a>).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec24">Resequencing of genotypes.</h3><p>WGRS was used for 29 elite varieties and RAD-sequencing was used for 61 genotypes (<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/nbt.2491#MOESM2">Supplementary Table 1</a>). For WGRS, separately indexed sequencing libraries were prepared for each genotype using Illumina TruSeq library kits (Illumina) and were pooled together for 100 bp pair-end sequencing using established v3 chemistry methodologies on single lanes of an Illumina HiSeq 2000 flow-cell (Illumina). RAD-sequencing, with the standard protocol<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="Baird, N.A. et al. Rapid SNP discovery and genetic mapping using sequenced RAD markers. PLoS ONE 3, e3376 (2008)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3484">53</a></sup> was used for <i>Ape</i>kI-digested DNAs of 48 genotypes and on HindIII-digested DNAs of 24 genotypes on the Illumina HiSeq 2000 system. Subsequently, RAD-sequence data for 61 nonredundant genotypes (from <i>Ape</i>KI and HindIII) were compiled. The resulting sequence data were processed using Casava pipeline (Casava v1.8).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec25">Genetic diversity analysis.</h3><p>Sequence diversity analysis, including PCA, dendrogram, and diversity parameters θπ and θw, were measured as described<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Xu, X. et al. Resequencing 50 accessions of cultivated and wild rice yields markers for identifying agronomically important genes. Nat. Biotechnol. 30, 1005–1011 (2012)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3502">54</a></sup>. F<sub>ST</sub> values for 31 elite cultivars and 25 landraces were calculated by using population branch statistics<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Xia, Q. et al. Complete resequencing of 40 genomes reveals domestication events and genes in silkworm (Bombyx). Science 326, 433–436 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3508">55</a></sup> and these values were compared using FDIST<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Beaumont, M.A. &amp; Nichols, R.A. Evaluating loci for use in the genetic analysis of population structure. Proc. R. Soc. Lond. B 263, 1619–1626 (1996)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3512">28</a></sup>. This approach has been found to be effective in identifying recent artificial selection considering the very short divergence time between landraces and elite cultivars<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Xia, Q. et al. Complete resequencing of 40 genomes reveals domestication events and genes in silkworm (Bombyx). Science 326, 433–436 (2009)." href="/articles/nbt.2491#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d38476e3516">55</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec26">Accession code.</h3><p>Genome sequence assembly and annotation data, NCBI Genome: <a href="http://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/bioproject/?term=PRJNA175619">PRJNA175619</a>.</p></div></div></section>

                        class="js-separator">, </span><span>Hideki Nagasaki</span></li><li><span

                        class="js-separator">, </span><span>Shoko Hikosaka</span></li><li><span
                        class="js-separator">, </span><span>Eiji Goto</span></li><li><span
                        class="js-separator">, </span><span>Kazuki Saito</span></li><li><span
                        class="js-separator">&nbsp;&amp;&nbsp;</span><span>Mami Yamazaki</span></li></ul>
              
              <p class="c-article-further-reading__journal-title" id="journal-name-5">
                <i>Nature Communications</i>
                (2021)
              </p>
            </li>
          
        </ul>
      </div>
    </div>
    </section>
